So here, since we are returning to the topic of what they are working on (which was briefly introduced earlier), I have used "hablando de" instead of using a literal translation like "iniciando con". <NL> - In Spanish, you use "llevan" when talking about someone carrying something with their hands. However, given that the soldier is carrying weight on his back, I chose to use the expression "carry on their backs" and translated it as "en sus espaldas". If we were to use a more literal translation like "están llevando sobre sus hombros", the meaning would not be incorrect, but it would convey that the soldier is carrying the weight on his shoulders. <NL> - I have kept the phrase "are being asked" as a single phrase in Spanish because it sounds more natural than splitting it into two phrases: "son preguntados para llevar más equipo". In English, we can use this expression to express that someone is obligated or expected to do something, and I think it's important to convey that sense of obligation in the translation.
